    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_582830142" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/582830142" />
    <a title="Harry" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7597429-harry"><img alt="Harry" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1380595404p2/7597429.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/582830142?book_show_action=true">Apr 06, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Harry" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Harry" href="/user/show/7597429-harry">Harry</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7597429-harry?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer582830142" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer510964915746977678">This is not a novel I would compliment for it's stylistic prose, its character development, or it's originality in terms of plot: this is a novel that were it to be true is nothing short of a devastating indictment of the War on drugs. My rating of this book is based on its subject matter and its research and how it affects me as a reader.<br/><br/>Normally, I throw up my eyebrows in quizzical fashion when reading reviews that complain about the lack of verisimilitude, or that the author somehow has inven</span>
  <span id="freeText510964915746977678" style="display:none">This is not a novel I would compliment for it's stylistic prose, its character development, or it's originality in terms of plot: this is a novel that were it to be true is nothing short of a devastating indictment of the War on drugs. My rating of this book is based on its subject matter and its research and how it affects me as a reader.<br /><br />Normally, I throw up my eyebrows in quizzical fashion when reading reviews that complain about the lack of verisimilitude, or that the author somehow has invented something in the reader's hometown that isn't true and therefore the whole novel is to be ridiculed and cast aside. It's fiction, the stuff's made up, folks! If you want realism, all the facts checked, then view your favorite documentary, or news column (not that facts are checked in the news), or gain your verisimilitude from reality TV! The beauty in art, as well as fiction, is that the author presents a view that is NOT as the world is. So, get over it.<br /><br />Having said that, if this novel's painstaking research is any indication (last count, the author spent 6 years doing research to pull this one off - that's 2,190 days) then what you will read will floor you. I say this if even a fraction of it is true. So, though fictionalized competently if not expertly, this book is about reality.<br /><br />Some reviewers call it Winslow's best, some his second best: with <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/8008928.Savages__Savages___1_" title="Savages (Savages, #1) by Don Winslow" rel="nofollow noopener">Savages</a> and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/164760.The_Winter_of_Frankie_Machine" title="The Winter of Frankie Machine by Don Winslow" rel="nofollow noopener">The Winter of Frankie Machine</a> as the contenders. For myself, coming to this second Winslow book after reading the first in the Neal Carey series: <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/243362.A_Cool_Breeze_on_the_Underground__Neal_Carey__1_" title="A Cool Breeze on the Underground (Neal Carey #1) by Don Winslow" rel="nofollow noopener">A Cool Breeze on the Underground</a> I can easily declare <i>The Power of the Dog</i> to be his best. With over 520 pages, it far surpasses the only other book I've read of Winslow's.<br /><br />So, I'm not going to talk about prose, setting, or the book's stylistic shortcomings. It's useless. Winslow has me in a corner because the subject matter is so devastating that it commands our attention every step of the way. The only thing to discuss is the veracity of what this novel is about and our opinion as readers of that truth. And if there's praise to be gifted to this novelist, than that praise belongs to Winslow for allowing us to see the consequences of the War on Drugs as seen through the eyes of the innocent and the not-so-innocent: the 3 or 4 fictional characters we follow across 3 decades.<br /><br />What is a War on Drugs? What is war? This is what I got from the book:<br /><br />War should be understood as <i>political violence</i>. We are obviously not actually waging a war on drugs. Drugs can't wage war. Drugs sit in plastic wrapping, or in a crack pipe. Ok. so who, then? Who or what are we waging war against? And why don't we call this war for what it really is? A political cold war that never ends. A war where the proliferation of hard drugs in our streets is the last thing of consequence. Drugs equals money, and money finances political violence. That is what Winslow tells me. <br /><br />But the collateral damage! I've heard that...that every war has them. But there's a difference between collateral damage that can't be avoided, and pure brutality for the sake of brutality. I find it horrific. <br /><br />This book is about sociopaths and psychopaths in power... what they will do to keep an idea away from this border while working for the U.S. government and against it. Winslow proves to us that ethics is only possible if you have a choice: faced with violence there is no such thing as ethics. There is a line between collateral damage and terrorism; and that line is drawn for the reader. And it is who steps across that line that floors you.<br /><br />And, so I think it's in this epic span of 3 decades, within this collateral damage that Winslow finds a chilling home for his novel and it's main characters. <br /><br />Fascinating book...I thought. </span>
  <a data-text-id="510964915746977678" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_3535438327" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3535438327" />
    <a title="Barry" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/22664741-barry"><img alt="Barry" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1375203200p2/22664741.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3535438327?book_show_action=true">Sep 24, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Barry" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Barry" href="/user/show/22664741-barry">Barry</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/8257329-the-power-of-the-dog">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3535438327" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8519629768580667520">The so-called "war on drugs" ineffectively took place over many years, starting with the Nixon administration. In fact, in January, 1970, along with a couple of graduate school buddies, I took a car trip through much of Mexico. When we returned to the US, the customs guys at the border took well over an hour to search our car, an innocuous red VW bug. <br/><br/>The Power of the Dog is an historical novel that follows that so-called war. The main characters are a Drug Enforcement officer, a CIA agent, a Ma</span>
  <span id="freeText8519629768580667520" style="display:none">The so-called "war on drugs" ineffectively took place over many years, starting with the Nixon administration. In fact, in January, 1970, along with a couple of graduate school buddies, I took a car trip through much of Mexico. When we returned to the US, the customs guys at the border took well over an hour to search our car, an innocuous red VW bug. <br /><br />The Power of the Dog is an historical novel that follows that so-called war. The main characters are a Drug Enforcement officer, a CIA agent, a Mafia under boss, a contract killer from NYC, a California prostitute, a Mexican drug lord and his enforcer brother and a literal cast thousands of supporting roles. <br /><br />Winslow does a brilliant job of weaving these characters and the events that they brought about together over a many year period. In fact, there was so much going on that it was difficult to follow everything. I suspect that whatever confusion I experienced had more to do with my failing neuronal processing than the complexity of the book. <br /><br />If one takes Winslow's writing to heart, several things about the war on drugs became abundantly clear. The level of viciousness, corruption and profit was extraordinary on all sides. The level of competence (and in many cases, nonchalance) on the part of various US government and law enforcement agencies was almost nonexistent. <br /><br />Winslow does a brilliant job in bringing this period to life in a raw, colorful, intense and realistic manner. He varies his prose according to the characters and setting. He uses dialogue brilliantly to provide, not just the plot, the action and the character but the atmosphere and the extent to which it was emotionally charged. <br /><br />The book is long - sometimes seeming as long as the so-called war itself - and occasionally became a real effort but those periods were always brief and, on balance, it was well worth the ride.<br /><br />The End</span>
  <a data-text-id="8519629768580667520" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1615447637" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1615447637" />
    <a title="Lawyer" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3025547-lawyer"><img alt="Lawyer" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1603672493p2/3025547.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1615447637?book_show_action=true">Apr 19, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lawyer" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lawyer" href="/user/show/3025547-lawyer">Lawyer</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780099464983" href="/book/show/1383999.The_Power_of_the_Dog">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3025547-lawyer?shelf=revenge">revenge</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3025547-lawyer?shelf=crime">crime</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3025547-lawyer?shelf=2016">2016</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3025547-lawyer?shelf=mexico">mexico</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3025547-lawyer?shelf=war-on-drugs">war-on-drugs</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3025547-lawyer?shelf=drug-cartels">drug-cartels</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3025547-lawyer?shelf=columbia">columbia</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3025547-lawyer?shelf=dea">dea</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3025547-lawyer?shelf=cia">cia</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3025547-lawyer?shelf=iran-contra-hearings">iran-contra-hearings</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1615447637" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6118647202133097866"><b>The Power of the Dog: Machismo, Madness, & Morality</b><br/><br/><a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/37795.Don_Winslow' title='Don Winslow' rel='nofollow noopener'>Don Winslow</a> has written the epic "Dope" novel in <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/1383999.The_Power_of_the_Dog' title='The Power of the Dog by Don Winslow' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Power of the Dog</a>. It is a mean, dirty story where it is not always easy to tell the good guys from the bad guys.<br/><br/>This is not a mere cop and crime story. Winslow goes much deeper than that. While not strictly historical fiction, because Winslow tends to change the names to protect the guilty, and omit the names to blur which Presidential Administration particular acts may be attributed to, consi</span>
  <span id="freeText6118647202133097866" style="display:none"><b>The Power of the Dog: Machismo, Madness, &amp; Morality</b><br /><br /><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/37795.Don_Winslow" title="Don Winslow" rel="nofollow noopener">Don Winslow</a> has written the epic "Dope" novel in <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/1383999.The_Power_of_the_Dog" title="The Power of the Dog by Don Winslow" rel="nofollow noopener">The Power of the Dog</a>. It is a mean, dirty story where it is not always easy to tell the good guys from the bad guys.<br /><br />This is not a mere cop and crime story. Winslow goes much deeper than that. While not strictly historical fiction, because Winslow tends to change the names to protect the guilty, and omit the names to blur which Presidential Administration particular acts may be attributed to, consider this a sweeping look at "The War on Drugs" from the founding days of the Drug Enforcement Administration in the mid-1970s to the end of the Nineties. <br /><br />Winslow's protagonist is Art Keller, a Vietnam Veteran. More fitting for having been an intel operative in the Phoenix Program during the Vietnam War, the program for the assassination of suspected Viet Cong leaders. Keller is not regular army. He is CIA.<br /><br />When the Drug Enforcement Administration was founded in the Seventies, many former Vietnam vets found themselves recruited into DEA ranks, including former CIA operatives. They found themselves on the outside, at odds with other law enforcement who had not been recruited from the Vietnam experience. Known as "Cowboys," they were spurned by their civilian counterparts and locked out of intel and operations when possible.<br /><br />Art Keller finds himself "Locked out" by his supervisor Tim Taylor who has stationed him in Mexico to shut down the heroin trade. But Keller has something going for him Taylor hasn't counted on. Keller's mother was a Latina. Essentially abandoned by his gringo father as he grew up in the barrio, Keller understands what it means to be Mexican. By apparent luck he finds himself in the boxing ring as the sparring partner of Cesar Barrerra, managed by brothers Raul and Adan. Keller is accepted. And wouldn't you know it, Tio, Uncle, Miguel Angel Barrerra, is a ranking Mexican police official who leads Keller to credit in shutting down the heroin traffic in Mexico and killing the heroin kingpin.<br /><br />Here's the complication. Tio has a motive. Keller was actually a tool. Tio Barrerra establishes a Federacion to distribute cocaine the up and coming drug to the streets of the United States. Enter the Columbian Drug Cartels. Enter the Mafia Connection. Oops. Enter the Contra Connection. Uh-oh. Enter the CIA support of the Contras who are under indictment for Trafficking Cocaine.<br /><br />Faster than you can say Ollie North, here portrayed as Major Scott Craig, Art Keller finds himself caught between the CIA and the Barerras fighting the good fight in the war on drugs. However the Barrerras are always just one step ahead of him.<br /><br />The key to any good narcotics investigation is the development of intel. Best source? Informants. However, now one tips on the Barrerras. It will get you killed. Keller gets antsy and practical. Following Tio Barrerra, he discovers Tio has taken a young lover and an apartment as a secret love nest. In a "Say it ain't so Keller" moment, Art plants an illegal bug. The intel is golden. On the basis of information received from a "reliable confidential informant" Keller begins to do serious damage to the Barrerra Operation.<br /><br />Keller has two partners, one, Ernie Hidalgo, kidnapped by the Barrerras. Hidalgo is brutally tortured to discover the identity of Keller's informant. Of course, Hidalgo doesn't know. In the process of the torture Hidalgo dies.<br /><br />What results is the ultimate vengeance tale. Keller is out to get the Barrerras. The Barrerras are out to get Keller. At the same time there are forces at work to shut Keller up as well. For reasons having nothing to do with his mission to avenge the death of his partner.<br /><br />Winslow will keep you on the edge of your seat. He provides you with a cast of characters and story reminiscent of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/22034.The_Godfather" title="The Godfather by Mario Puzo" rel="nofollow noopener">The Godfather</a>, but with the intensity of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/380364.Dog_Soldiers" title="Dog Soldiers by Robert Stone" rel="nofollow noopener">Dog Soldiers</a> by <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/41938.Robert_Stone" title="Robert Stone" rel="nofollow noopener">Robert Stone</a>.<br /><br />This is the thinking reader's dope novel. It is a novel of morality, ethics, and the ease with which those essentials may be lost. Save us from the power of the dog.<br /><br /><blockquote>14 I am poured out like water, and all my bones are out of joint: my heart is like wax; it is melted in the midst of my bowels.<br /><br />15 My strength is dried up like a potsherd; and my tongue cleaveth to my jaws; and thou hast brought me into the dust of death.<br /><br />16 For dogs have compassed me: the assembly of the wicked have inclosed me: they pierced my hands and my feet.<br /><br />17 I may tell all my bones: they look and stare upon me.<br /><br />18 They part my garments among them, and cast lots upon my vesture.<br /><br />19 But be not thou far from me, O Lord: O my strength, haste thee to help me.<br /><br />20 Deliver my soul from the sword; my darling from the power of the dog.<br /><br />21 Save me from the lion's mouth<br /><br />Psalm 22, KJV</blockquote></span>
  <a data-text-id="6118647202133097866" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2025495735" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2025495735" />
    <a title="Dave" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/35045983-dave"><img alt="Dave" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1496413985p2/35045983.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2025495735?book_show_action=true">Jun 10, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Dave" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Dave" href="/user/show/35045983-dave">Dave</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/35045983-dave?shelf=100-top-crime-fiction">100-top-crime-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/35045983-dave?shelf=crime-fiction-all">crime-fiction-all</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2025495735" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7770044227160112665">The Power of the Dog is a big, sweeping, epic tale. It is only 560 pages long and I say only because this novel is so intoxicatingly good that it is difficult to put it aside even for a moment. It is a novel not just about the drug war against the Mexican cartels, based loosely on real events, but it is a story about all kinds of people caught up in the war from the DEA agents who lost their regular lives, but not their souls, to the young kids who grew up to be killers, both on the streets of H</span>
  <span id="freeText7770044227160112665" style="display:none">The Power of the Dog is a big, sweeping, epic tale. It is only 560 pages long and I say only because this novel is so intoxicatingly good that it is difficult to put it aside even for a moment. It is a novel not just about the drug war against the Mexican cartels, based loosely on real events, but it is a story about all kinds of people caught up in the war from the DEA agents who lost their regular lives, but not their souls, to the young kids who grew up to be killers, both on the streets of Hell’s Kitchen and in the barrios of San Diego and Tijuana. It is a novel that talks about the brutal corruption of Mexican politics and the compromised culture of just about everything because of the drug money and violence and about all the people swept up into it and the victims of the ever-growing violence.<br /><br />It is a story that is at times critical of the War on Drugs, citing it as ineffective, compromised by other interests such as funneling weapons and dollars against Communist incursions into Central America and Colombia. It is a story about how difficult it has been to control this situation which has grown more and more out of control. But, the novel tells the story not as a news account but as a fictional story with real characters who have real connections to each other and histories and cultures. Winslow traces the history of these characters from their early years as they cross paths time and time again. DEA Agent Art Keller is the star of the novel and he meets frustration time and time again as his goal of removing the head of the snake is frustrated time and time again by politics and corruption and dirty dealings. This is an incredibly well-written, richly drawn, novel that is worth more than one read.</span>
  <a data-text-id="7770044227160112665" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_3354243603" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3354243603" />
    <a title="Brendan Monroe" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/22409011-brendan-monroe"><img alt="Brendan Monroe" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1565543383p2/22409011.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3354243603?book_show_action=true">Jun 08, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Brendan Monroe" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Brendan Monroe" href="/user/show/22409011-brendan-monroe">Brendan Monroe</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/22409011-brendan-monroe?shelf=america">america</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/22409011-brendan-monroe?shelf=audiobook">audiobook</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/22409011-brendan-monroe?shelf=death-drugs-and-political-corrupt">death-drugs-and-political-corrupt</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/22409011-brendan-monroe?shelf=great-narrator">great-narrator</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3354243603" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6176244306463603395">While technically fiction, "The Power of the Dog" is a pretty accurate account of the disastrous War on Drugs. Like the "War on Terror" that followed it, the War on Drugs is the result of corrupt mismanagement, inadequate policies, and an unclear objective. It was lost from the word go, in other words.<br/><br/>I picked up "The Power of the Dog" because I've heard from all corners that Don Winslow's recently completed Cartel Trilogy is the bee's knees, which is say, astoundingly good, so I started at the </span>
  <span id="freeText6176244306463603395" style="display:none">While technically fiction, "The Power of the Dog" is a pretty accurate account of the disastrous War on Drugs. Like the "War on Terror" that followed it, the War on Drugs is the result of corrupt mismanagement, inadequate policies, and an unclear objective. It was lost from the word go, in other words.<br /><br />I picked up "The Power of the Dog" because I've heard from all corners that Don Winslow's recently completed Cartel Trilogy is the bee's knees, which is say, astoundingly good, so I started at the beginning as one is generally meant to do. <br /><br />This is a very good start. There are moments when the larger story feels occasionally at risk of serving as a set piece for the action sequences, but Winslow always comes through in the end to redirect the narrative. <br /><br />This is largely rich, hugely compelling stuff, absolutely necessary reading for those who don't understand how buying drugs in the US indirectly leads to death and terror being inflicted upon innocent civilians on the other side of the border. It should make you think twice about the origins of everything we consume.<br /><br />As for the story, think "The Godfather" crossed with "Traffic," "Sicario," and "The Wire." Sounds pretty good, right? <br /><br />If we were an adult country, we wouldn't prohibit any drugs. Boom — the cartels go away. Do what certain European countries have done, limit drug use to certain areas, require hard-core drug users to shoot up under supervision, funnel the trillions we spend on doomed efforts like the War on Drugs towards education, community outreach, and mental health programs to give people a sense of purpose so they won't turn towards drugs in the first place. <br /><br />Looking now at the full scope of the problem, one can't help but ask, how in the hell did we fuck this up?</span>
  <a data-text-id="6176244306463603395" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1227887239" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1227887239" />
    <a title="Steve" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1254714-steve"><img alt="Steve" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1513279210p2/1254714.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1227887239?book_show_action=true">Mar 15, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Steve" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Steve" href="/user/show/1254714-steve">Steve</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1254714-steve?shelf=crime-badness-noir">crime-badness-noir</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1227887239" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10464059639177114276">This one started out great, but with about 150 pages to go (it's well over 500), I found my interest waning. Characters started flattening out, repetitive gun battles where it seemed the major characters had an almost hobbit-like ability to survive, and a general sense of looseness as the epic subject (the drug wars) seemed to go beyond Winslow's pulpish grasp. There are a number of awesome, blood soaked scenes. A favorite of mine was early on where an Irish enforcer tries to lean too hard on a </span>
  <span id="freeText10464059639177114276" style="display:none">This one started out great, but with about 150 pages to go (it's well over 500), I found my interest waning. Characters started flattening out, repetitive gun battles where it seemed the major characters had an almost hobbit-like ability to survive, and a general sense of looseness as the epic subject (the drug wars) seemed to go beyond Winslow's pulpish grasp. There are a number of awesome, blood soaked scenes. A favorite of mine was early on where an Irish enforcer tries to lean too hard on a couple of teenagers in a bar. Bad move. There's another scene or scenes, involving a mother (and her children), running away from her drug dealer husband, in order to be with her thought-to-be lover, that is about about as cruel as anything I've ever read. In other words, Winslow can definitely push your buttons, and at his best, he has an ear for dialogue that is often reminiscent of Elmore Leonard. When he's not at his best, cliches start popping up, and plotting gets clunky. In particular, there is a long Mexican Day-of-the-Dead sequence that I found incredibly awkward. It recalls the operatic kill-offs from the Godfather movies, but it lacks their cohesion and flair. It was then that I knew the wheels had come off. It was also around then that Winslow seemed to be relying more and more on the actual history of the drug wars to push the novel, and its fictional characters, along. When that goes beyond a certain point, your characters begin to hollow out and become cartoons or pieces to move around. You no longer care. At least I didn't. <br /><br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="10464059639177114276" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3128281-renee-itsbooktalk?shelf=all-time-favorites">all-time-favorites</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3078288374" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3542755127883105701">When I finished reading and couldn’t stop thinking about American Dirt recently, I knew I wanted to read more on the subject of Mexico and cartels . I grabbed the audio and ebook (I like to alternate) and promptly became obsessed with the story of DEA agent Art Keller and drug lord Adan Barrera. Although this epic saga revolves around them, their initial friendship followed by hatred, the cast of supporting characters is vast but each person felt real & everyone was flawed!<br/>~<br/>This book will NOT be</span>
  <span id="freeText3542755127883105701" style="display:none">When I finished reading and couldn’t stop thinking about American Dirt recently, I knew I wanted to read more on the subject of Mexico and cartels . I grabbed the audio and ebook (I like to alternate) and promptly became obsessed with the story of DEA agent Art Keller and drug lord Adan Barrera. Although this epic saga revolves around them, their initial friendship followed by hatred, the cast of supporting characters is vast but each person felt real &amp; everyone was flawed!<br />~<br />This book will NOT be for everyone as it is violent in parts- there is so much murder, and some involved children but there would be no way to tell this story without these details as this is the reality of what’s been happening in Mexico for years. After I finished reading I watched interviews with Winslow and sadly the murders in this book are based on true events. ⠀⠀<br />~<br />That being said, this is one of the best crime thrillers I’ve ever read! Winslow’s writing is propulsive, raw, and unflinching and reads as if you’re watching a movie - which this trilogy has been optioned for- with levels of suspense and tension that kept me reading late into the night. PS the audio is amazing </span>
  <a data-text-id="3542755127883105701" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1788075294" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9063459981884393282">Many reviews already written and a comprehensive synopsis on offer already. Thoroughly enjoyed this gritty, violent novel about the quest for power in the drug wars between the U.S.A and South America. The action takes place between the 1970's and late 1990's. It quite an intense read in places. Really no winners here and often difficult to know who the "good guys" are meant to be. Saw this recommended by author Adrian McKinty on his blog and decided to check it out. Very glad I did.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3325448880?book_show_action=true">Jun 07, 2020</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/11227317-the-power-of-the-dog">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5456932-tony?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3325448880" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2128621438159050549">I know it’s a cliche but this really is a rollercoaster of a book. It’s absolutely relentless, epic in its scope and cinematic in its delivery. It’s also cleverly written with lots of different and distinct “voices” - the dogged DEA agent, merciless drug-lords, mobsters, hitmen... The only thing that stops it being a five-star book, in my view, is that its relentless pace leaves insufficient time for character development. But it’s a fair trade-off. </span>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('OixaGqBFx8STsvbp4zocRz4QAlTN7eVHnAkpPpgViJicig7Nq9m4pTvRTCjlbVQlBvsv7uAY4NJe6/kpmVNt6w==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('QkOUjIYaNT1+T7aVGUoX+GuA2tXdoG9Cx8L0o0orRODk5cBbjYZKXNYsDFQfHV+aU2v3b/BVatcFICS0S22hkw==')})
  }

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer9640493493122240849">Don Winslow is the author of twenty-one acclaimed, award-winning international bestsellers, including the <i>New York Times</i> bestsellers <i>The Force</i> and <i>The Border</i>, the #1 international bestseller <i>The Cartel, The Power of the Dog, Savages</i>, and <i>The Winter of Frankie Machine</i>. <i>Savages</i> was made into a feature film by three-time Oscar-winning writer-director Oliver Stone. <i>The Power of the Dog, The Cartel</i> and</span>
  <span id="freeText9640493493122240849" style="display:none">Don Winslow is the author of twenty-one acclaimed, award-winning international bestsellers, including the <i>New York Times</i> bestsellers <i>The Force</i> and <i>The Border</i>, the #1 international bestseller <i>The Cartel, The Power of the Dog, Savages</i>, and <i>The Winter of Frankie Machine</i>. <i>Savages</i> was made into a feature film by three-time Oscar-winning writer-director Oliver Stone. <i>The Power of the Dog, The Cartel</i> and <i>The Border</i> sold to FX in a major multimillion-dollar deal to air as a weekly television series beginning in 2020. <br /><br />A former investigator, antiterrorist trainer and trial consultant, Winslow lives in California and Rhode Island.<br /><br /><br /><i>Librarian Note: There is more than one author in the GoodReads database with this name. <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/topic/show_group/44217.Master_List_of_Author_Disambiguation_by_Spaces" rel="nofollow noopener">See this thread for more information</a>.</i><br /></span>
